<user>100135586375859316160< /user><user_name>Taylor Woods< /user_name><Time>1465689475658<//Time><Rating>4</Rating>< text>
Los Arroyos offers a good selection of cuisine, including both traditional items, as well as more typical "Mexican food" dining experience. The dining room is small, has ample natural light, and comfortable seating.  Service is fast-casual, with counter ordering and table delivery.

I have enjoyed several of their dishes, including the burritos, chimichangas,  and several dinner "specialties." Their molcajete is quite good. Food is neither bland nor too spicy, and the flavor strikes a good medium to appeal to a broad plate.

As a local, this is one of the few establishments I frequent in the outlet mall area, as I typically try to avoid crowds and traffic.</text>

<rating>3</rating><Text>First of all, the food here is excellent. It is without question the best Mexican food in Camarillo (don't let it go to your head, that's like the best pork chop in Riyadh- Camarillo is a restaurant wasteland). The ingredients are all high quality and the taste is outstanding. I rate it higher than the Montecito location.

Second, this is not a place that caters to locals. It's in the Outlet Mall and likely does not see its customers again.

Which is why I gave them 3 stars and not the five they should get. The food is very over priced. I'm always willing to pay more for good food but $14. for nachos is over the top. I've been going since they opened and the plate of nachos I got today was exactly half of their normal portion. My go to dish at Los Arroyos is the molcajete which is always terrific. Today it was 2/3 the size and they eliminated the shrimp. They've stopped giving chips with their entrees now as well.

I know their target customer is the one time tourist. As much as I enjoy the food, I can't justify small portions and high prices just because they're catering to the tourist/shopper trade and not the loyalty of locals.<//Text>< Pics>

I have a storage unit at a CubeSmart in Las Vegas and the difference between that one and this one are night and day. Firstly, the units at this facility cost double the price of the ones I have in Las Vegas. Additionally, the CubeSmart in Las Vegas is ran by kind and helpful staff who go out of their way to make sure your are well accommodated. The staff here are not only unhelpful, they are just flat out rude - constant attitude and random snarky comments. The facility was not clean once in the entire time I stored there - grimey elevators and nasty bathrooms. The worst was that the staff was so lazy that, rather than clean the restrooms, they put up signs on every restroom saying that they were "broken". While I don't write a lot of reviews, I felt compelled to offer praise when someone/something exceeds expectations. The CubeSmart company, Manager Lizbeth Prado, and General Manager Krista Rangel did just that.

I initially began my "storage experience" with Public Storage, and it was terrible. After a couple months of worrying about my stuff without a temperature controlled climate, a poor office manager who hates her job named Sheila, and run-down storage compartments, I decided it was time to move. I found a CubeSmart near me, and the reviews looked good. Although I had never heard of the company, I decided to give them a look.

Upon entering CubeSmart, the facilities were clean, video monitors were on and working, the units were temperature controlled, and the prices were affordable. The manager I worked with was Lizbeth Prado, and she was AWESOME! She was friendly, super helpful, and got a me a rate that made the hassle of moving all my stuff (again) worth it.

CubeSmart is a wonderful place for storage, and this company has exceeded my expectations for what a storage company should be. They set the bar for excellence.

Thanks to CubeSmart Self-Storage, I will assuredly be using you again with storage needs in the future.

Thanks Lizbeth and Krista! You managers are STELLAR.

From,
A Guy Who Moved Twice & It Was Worth It< /Review>

<date>1466044597320< /date>< rate>

<Text>Don't go here if you are planning to get a good deal or any deal for that matter!

I called in to ask if they sold Eternal Masters Booster packs / boxes and was given a price that was double the price of every other competitor both nearby as well as online. When asked why the price was so steep the manager told me it was because their "magic specialist" had recommended that price and it is set in stone. I asked afterwards if it was possible to get some sort of a deal on the packs or boxes if I bought a large quantity and was immediately told (I did not even get a chance to speak an offer) , "nope the price is set" and "I am the manager and these prices is what were going with, people will buy them at these high of a price and so therefor this is what I will sell it at".

I understand you can't always expect to get a haggled price , but when a store marks up a product nearly TWICE that of any other competitor you would think there is some wiggle room or perhaps a better explanation than "I am the manager, this is the price."

Also one friendly tip (I could give so much more but I will highlight this one), don't tell someone "I don't know anything about magic but my specialist has recommended we sell for this price" and then begin to get upset when I ask to speak with the specialist.

It is no surprise that all the other stores nearby as well as online are able to sell their booster packs / boxes when all of them are nice and well knowledgeable about the prices of magic.< /Text>< Pictures>
None</Pictures>

I was referred to this place by my insurance and didn't have many options.  The doctors and assistants are nice enough but the office is tremendously over booked.  It's difficult to tell if the people there cant do their job or they are overworked and/or a combination.  To get a call in is nearly impossible.  If you do get a call in, expect to be on hold for at least 30 minutes or longer.  When you actually show up at the office, your expect to be seen at least 30 minutes after your appointment time but most likely closer to 45-60 minutes.  This is only for your vitals to be taken, then you are sent to a second waiting room to wait for a room to be seen.  A visit that should take no more then 30 minutes takes anywhere between 90-120 minutes.  The doctors there are not there daily, apparently 1-2 days at most so it is very difficult to get an appointment and then to change it is impossible.  If you get sent to get some labworks done, MRI, CT scan, etc make sure to have a copy with you because they never seem to have the results from the labs.  There also appears be bad communication between the doctors because when my staples where to be taken out he did not know if my surgical drain was to be taken out.  I had to wait a couple of hours to see if this was going to be done.  The owners of this medical center need to get more people to work at their location.  Also, they have parking but they never had any parking available and please make sure to have your copay ready because that they do request almost immediately upon checking in with the clinic.</Text>

<user_id>115613434754347882378</user_id><Name>Sean Jackson</Name>< time>
1562109828328</time>
< rate>
5< /rate>
<review>Having lived just down the road from this Signal Hill institution for more than 15 years, it's odd that only after having moved a few miles away I would be drawn in to routinely dining here.  So, what's up you ask? For years  My parents and some good friends of theirs have made Wednesday evenings at Curley's apart of their routine. Although often invited, It was so routine that nothing seemed pressing about joining them. That was until my fine folks retired to Oregon and now seeing them was far less often and no longer on a whim the way I was used too. So, when they came to town and were wrapped up in catching up with old friends you can bet that Wednesday evening they were heading to Curley's. This was an invite I couldn't pass up, and now more than ever understand how good company, along with excellent food, served by one heck of a personable waiter named Jason and awesome live entertainment for a reasonable amount were so compelling. This is traditional diner food served in portions and prepared in a way you don't find often these days. The entertainment is usually a duet banjo and tuba with vocals from both mixed in. Usually American standards from the 1920's (roaring 20's) with sing a longs (lyrics provided to every table), the crowd of anywhere from 20 to 60 people are welcoming and a jovial bunch, and the atmosphere is so infectious it's impossible to imagine anybody not joining in for a thundering chorus of "she'll be coming round the mountain, when she comes". On evenings when the duet isn't available they are covered by the likes of a very talented Barbershop Quartet, or a sit in artist. But if this kind of "all in" audience participation live entertainment isn't exactly your thing, no need to hesitate; the front dining room and bar are left to the charms of what ever commentary patrons may have to what ever sports game is being aired on the TV monitors where there is no expectation of participation. The food and service are well worth giving Curley's a try. I regret waiting over 15 years to find out.< /review><Pictures>None</Pictures>< Response>
None<//Response>
